  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_55df541e-01e8-4790-8ef0-054525c8ddc5'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer14158097024277528760">For years, tales of<br/><br/><strong>DRAGONS</strong><br/><br/>from another world kidnapping and enslaving humans have been circulating in Jason Masters’ world, while for a slave girl named Koren, the stories of a human world seem pure myth.   <span id="freeText14158097024277528760" style="display:none">For years, tales of<br /><br /><strong>DRAGONS</strong><br /><br />from another world kidnapping and enslaving humans have been circulating in Jason Masters’ world, while for a slave girl named Koren, the stories of a human world seem pure myth. Together, these two teens will need to bridge two planets in order to overthrow the draconic threat and bring the lost slaves home.<br /><br /><strong>What if the Legends Are True?</strong><br /><br />Jason Masters doubted the myths that told of people taken through a portal to another realm and enslaved by dragons. But when he receives a cryptic message from his missing brother, he must uncover the truth and find the portal before it’s too late. At the same time, Koren, a slave in the dragons’ realm, discovers she has a gift that could either save or help doom her people. As Jason and Koren work to rescue the enslaved humans, a mystic prophecy surrounding a black egg may make all their efforts futile.</span>

<div id="review_138016032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138016032" />
    <a title="Kayt O&#39;Bibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3452501-kayt-o-bibliophile"><img alt="Kayt O&#39;Bibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274295868p2/3452501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138016032?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayt O&#39;Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayt O&#39;Bibliophile" href="/user/show/3452501-kayt-o-bibliophile">Kayt O&#39;Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3452501-kayt-o-bibliophile?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3452501-kayt-o-bibliophile?shelf=ugh-endings">ugh-endings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138016032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6257371160223536217">Jason Masters has trained his whole life, hearing the previously-unbelieved stories about dragons stealing humans and taking them to another world. Koren is a slave in the dragon's world, where any sign of disobedience equals death. Both passionately want to rescue the humans, but an old dragon prophecy stands in their way.<br/><br/>I would not have pegged this as being written by an established author; the problems are such that it felt like a new one in desperate need of editorial help or feedback. <br/><br/>The </span>
  <span id="freeText6257371160223536217" style="display:none">Jason Masters has trained his whole life, hearing the previously-unbelieved stories about dragons stealing humans and taking them to another world. Koren is a slave in the dragon's world, where any sign of disobedience equals death. Both passionately want to rescue the humans, but an old dragon prophecy stands in their way.<br /><br />I would not have pegged this as being written by an established author; the problems are such that it felt like a new one in desperate need of editorial help or feedback. <br /><br />The first problem is the setting. Davis does a <i>horrible</i> job of setting up Jason's world, the first one we're introduced to. Is it modern-day? The future? The past? Even once you finally get what it is (sci-fi setting; medieval-ish with technology for people in charge), it just doesn't fit well. There is a lot of <i>telling</i>, without the <i>showing</i> necessary for me to envision people, places, and events in my mind.<br /><br />Characters are another problem. The main characters all feel one-dimensional and uninteresting. Even the dragons, though they (and their world) get slightly better treatment.<br /><br />The book is the first in a quartet, but there's nothing to make you want the next book despite the fact that the story is nowhere near complete. You finish with a feeling of "I wasted my time on <i>that</i>?"</span>
  <a data-text-id="6257371160223536217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_107683173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107683173" />
    <a title="Jill Williamson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/955038-jill-williamson"><img alt="Jill Williamson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442498975p2/955038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107683173?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill Williamson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill Williamson" href="/user/show/955038-jill-williamson">Jill Williamson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107683173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4754756973729731145">Review by Jill Williamson<br/><br/>What if the legends are true?<br/><br/>Jason doubts the myths that people were once taken through a portal to another realm where dragons rule. But his brother gives him a message that proves something is wrong with the world he lives in. He snoops around, hoping to find out where his brother went and how he might get there too.<br/><br/>Meanwhile, Koren, a slave girl in the dragons’ realm, seeks the same kind of answers. Where did her people come from? Is what the dragons tell them true? O</span>
  <span id="freeText4754756973729731145" style="display:none">Review by Jill Williamson<br /><br />What if the legends are true?<br /><br />Jason doubts the myths that people were once taken through a portal to another realm where dragons rule. But his brother gives him a message that proves something is wrong with the world he lives in. He snoops around, hoping to find out where his brother went and how he might get there too.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Koren, a slave girl in the dragons’ realm, seeks the same kind of answers. Where did her people come from? Is what the dragons tell them true? Or were they really captives from another land? Koren tries to find out, and only her gift of being a Starlighter can save her from the truth she discovers.<br /><br />This was an interesting premise. It got off to a slow start, but I enjoyed how Davis weaved Jason and Koren’s stories together. I liked the dragon world, but this story left me with more questions than answers. There were lots of threads left hanging that, no doubt, Davis will tie up in the sequels, though I would have liked a little more resolution to this story. Bryan Davis fans will be thrilled with this new series and be clamoring for the sequel.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4754756973729731145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_141035643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141035643" />
    <a title="liirogue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/334806-liirogue"><img alt="liirogue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1191105513p2/334806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141035643?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="liirogue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="liirogue" href="/user/show/334806-liirogue">liirogue</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141035643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12752388932955898549">This story had a lot of potential, but it got lost in poor character and world development. Davis has set his story in another world and time, but he never brings it to life. I never felt immersed in this world or like I had any kind of sense of it. Add wooden, stereotypical characters and the author's penchant for dragging everything on way too long, and this plot never stood a chance.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3154339500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3154339500" />
    <a title="Anna Logan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99500952-anna-logan"><img alt="Anna Logan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579663173p2/99500952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3154339500?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Logan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Logan" href="/user/show/99500952-anna-logan">Anna Logan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3154339500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13650825935152583852">I read this series a few years ago as a fifteen-year-old. At the time, I was pretty enthralled--though I felt some character development and even just emotional depth was lacking, it was easy to gloss over that and get swept up in the intricate plot.<br/><br/>This time around, perhaps just because I'm older, I did not find it so easy to gloss over those issues.<br/><br/>Emotion is almost nonexistent in this book. A main character is reunited with a best friend he thought was dead, and the scene holds about as much </span>
  <span id="freeText13650825935152583852" style="display:none">I read this series a few years ago as a fifteen-year-old. At the time, I was pretty enthralled--though I felt some character development and even just emotional depth was lacking, it was easy to gloss over that and get swept up in the intricate plot.<br /><br />This time around, perhaps just because I'm older, I did not find it so easy to gloss over those issues.<br /><br />Emotion is almost nonexistent in this book. A main character is reunited with a best friend he thought was dead, and the scene holds about as much emotion as could be expected of two acquaintances running into each other at Walmart. I'm sorry to say it, but there truly is a painfully dull void where there should be feeling, tension, energy, and drama. <br /><br />There are some word choices and themes that are just...awkward. There is frequent and unnatural-feeling references to "warrior training" and "warrior skills". The wording used just doesn't sound right. It sounds artificial, and perhaps childish. This is a minor flaw of course, but it definitely distracts from the story.<br /><br />I will also say that I couldn't help being annoyed with how Elyssa is portrayed. With her Diviner abilities and cleverness, she is more than capable of leading and making decisions. Yet she usually follows whatever the present male character says and does. Or she strokes his ego, and/or acts like the damsel-in-distress, desperate for a gallant knight to hold her hand.<br /><br />The characters in general seem pretty flat. Arxad is the most intriguing character so far in the story, as he seems to occupy a gray area--good sometimes, bad others. But for the cast overall, it's hard to detect much personality or depth in any of them. Randall *almost* has a nice arc, starting out as dislikeable but becoming likeable by the end, but I would have liked to see it better developed.<br /><br />I haven't quite decided if I even want to continue reading the series. Most likely I will, since I own them, and I do remember being very impressed with the plot. So while I'm afraid I can't offer much praise for the book, I'm hopeful that memory serves true and the storyline, as I get deeper, will help make up for the lack of character development and emotional depth.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13650825935152583852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Usually, I analyze world building and characters and plot in my reviews, but honestly what stuck out to me was the unpredictability.<br /><br />Although I dragons and portals and a slightly insane old man do make for a fun book too. <br /><br />I was also very intrigued by the Starlighter's and the Diviner's abilities. Very interesting. <br /><br />Plot: Delightfully unpredictable<br />Writing: Could be stronger, but pretty good<br />Characters: It was a large cast, which made it difficult to create full arcs, but I suppose there are 3 books<br />Questionable Content: Dragon eats a person, sword fighting, murder, brief mentions of dragons forcing humans to breed, person almost gets burned alive, arrow gets removed from person, lots of magic, no real romance, no cussing.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_99157609" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99157609" />
    <a title="Jadewik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/152831-jadewik"><img alt="Jadewik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271977762p2/152831.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99157609?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jadewik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jadewik" href="/user/show/152831-jadewik">Jadewik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/152831-jadewik?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/152831-jadewik?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/152831-jadewik?shelf=firstreads-goodreads-giveaways">firstreads-goodreads-giveaways</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/152831-jadewik?shelf=i-owned">i-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99157609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6828912599803230395">Two planets on opposite sides of the solar system are connected by a gateway that has been closed for centuries. One planet whose natives call it Starlight is home to dragons who have enslaved humans from the planet Darksphere. (Humans call their planet Major Four and Starlight is referred to as Dracon.) Since the gateway between planets has been closed, much controversy exists on both planets as to the truth behind the stories of the humans who are enslaved by dragons (the Lost Ones). But when </span>
  <span id="freeText6828912599803230395" style="display:none">Two planets on opposite sides of the solar system are connected by a gateway that has been closed for centuries. One planet whose natives call it Starlight is home to dragons who have enslaved humans from the planet Darksphere. (Humans call their planet Major Four and Starlight is referred to as Dracon.) Since the gateway between planets has been closed, much controversy exists on both planets as to the truth behind the stories of the humans who are enslaved by dragons (the Lost Ones). But when Jason Masters stumbles into circumstances that force him towards the gateway, the adventure begins.<br /><br />This book has a lot going on all at once. That, I believe, made it quite entertaining. It starts out with a bang at the warrior championships. Right away you're introduced to the main character and some supporting characters. Immediately following the tournament, you're introduced to Koren, the other main character-- our Starlighter.<br /><br />The author does an excellent job introducing the background story-- how the Lost Ones were captured-- and developing it throughout the book. We find out early on the proximity of the planets through a poster on Adrian's wall. We also learn of the story through an underground newsletter and some of the finer points of plot, which I will refrain from revealing. <br /><br />I think it's really tricky for an author to balance events in two places at once and Bryan Davis did a fantastic job of keeping on par with events on both planets. There was also a lot of traveling in the book, but it wasn't bogged down with long descriptions of travel-- just descriptions of destinations, which were transitioned into quite well. Each event advanced the plot and left some interesting strands of plot dangling about for future use. (Some of those "danglers" include Jason's brothers and the Bear Jason and crew fought... plus what happened to several other characters whom were introduced.) This series has a lot of potential and a lot of things that could be tied together from this first book. I'm very interested in seeing where the author goes from here.<br /><br />I mostly enjoy the fact that this isn't the same old fantasy book with dragons that I've read time and time again. While the concept of a gateway has been done before (Stargate, for one popular example), I really thought the author put an interesting spin on it. Though, I did have a difficult time wrapping my head around the involvement of technology in both worlds-- Starlight seems to have so little by way of technology while Major Four has substantial technological advances... I found it slightly unbelievable when the photo gun was used later in the book, without any question or reaction from the Lost Ones. Do they have this same technology on Starlight? If so, why did the author not make the connection?<br /><br />Also... I really hope we get more information about that finger and its role in the books soon. It was really not used much in the plot of this book, except the heroic deeds that make it change colour. (Forgive me, review readers, for being so vague.)<br /><br />The only other thing I didn't like about this book was the brief introduction of Jason's brothers who are never mentioned again in the book... granted, there was a lot going on at the time, so I truly hope they'll be mentioned again in forthcoming books.<br /><br />I love the complexity and depth of some of the characters-- Arxad, for example, is quite the enigma. You have no idea what side he's on or what his agenda is throughout the whole book. The author tends to use him one-sided and only at the end do you wonder where he really stands.<br /><br />Koren, I have to say, I cannot stand as a character... but more because she's a character who I cannot relate to because she's so impulsive. I'm actually surprised at some of the situations she manages to squeak her way through... but I suppose that's the plus-side of being a Starlighter-- I'd explain, but that would kill most of the rising action of the book.<br /><br />Jason is also extremely impulsive... and really thick-headed. I also wonder how he survives... but I suppose that's teenage logic coming into play. If I went somewhere new, I'd look about a bit more than Jason. He just goes charging in like Leroy Jenkins in World of Warcraft. (Forgive the WoW reference. I blame my husband.)<br /><br />Those who don't like violence in books might want to avoid all the stabbing, blood, burnt bodies, drowning etc that is mentioned. The descriptions, though violent, aren't graphic. They are tastefully done. There is mention of "breeding" humans on Starlight... but aside from that, nothing to shy away from. I can't recall any swearing. Overall, I thought the book was pretty teen-reader friendly. <br /><br />So, ultimately, the plot isn't very complex but the story is paced well and has enough action and interesting plot points to keep the story entertaining. It's a good, quick candy read... and an enjoyable one too. If you like fantasy and dragons mixed with a little science and sword fighting, pick it up. It's worth the read. Though, I warn you... it really segues into the next book of the series and, though it stops at a good place, the story is still left hanging.<br /><br />To Meet FTC Guidelines, I'm disclosing that I won this book-- for free-- VIA Goodreads First Reads.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6828912599803230395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15881400115752850477">Interesting idea. But I can tell this is a book in a series because there are so many questions that are left unanswered. I feel like I am missing a prologue for this book, but I guess I just need to read book two to find out. Guess I was in a mood for a whole complete story with an optional book two to further the adventure. <br/><br/>Dragons, sword fights, but a mix of science (yes science, not magic)to bring you into a place between worlds, Starlight the Dragon Planet, and the Fourth Major the human pl</span>
  <span id="freeText15881400115752850477" style="display:none">Interesting idea. But I can tell this is a book in a series because there are so many questions that are left unanswered. I feel like I am missing a prologue for this book, but I guess I just need to read book two to find out. Guess I was in a mood for a whole complete story with an optional book two to further the adventure. <br /><br />Dragons, sword fights, but a mix of science (yes science, not magic)to bring you into a place between worlds, Starlight the Dragon Planet, and the Fourth Major the human planet. You have legends between both worlds, human enslavement under Dragon control on Starlight and a government keeping dragons as a myth on Fourth Major. <br /><br />Other than some confusion on how the science all played a part in this universe, I have to say that this book was a fun read, but only if you are looking for a series to get into. But it's got me hooked. If you want an interesting story involving our favorite fire breathing reptiles than by all means pick this book up. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1607758083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17103237243389721488">Something I've particularly enjoyed about this novel is how not one side sees history as legend--it's <i>both</i> sides who view the history of dragons/a world of freedom as legend. I like that the author took on this tactic because this made the story much more interesting, especially since most authors would've put that only one side viewed this history as legend whilst the other side knows the truth about history. Sometimes both sides have it tainted--a good view placed firmly here!<br/><br/>The author also m</span>
  <span id="freeText17103237243389721488" style="display:none">Something I've particularly enjoyed about this novel is how not one side sees history as legend--it's <i>both</i> sides who view the history of dragons/a world of freedom as legend. I like that the author took on this tactic because this made the story much more interesting, especially since most authors would've put that only one side viewed this history as legend whilst the other side knows the truth about history. Sometimes both sides have it tainted--a good view placed firmly here!<br /><br />The author also makes use of both dialogue and setting to set this story off, and does this in a very balanced way. I did enjoy this. However, I felt that the author should've put more imagery into this novel, though that's just my personal preference (any author can write any way they want, really, it doesn't matter).<br /><br />Overall, an interesting novel.</span>

<div id="review_1409570205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409570205" />
    <a title="Sic Transit Gloria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27914644-sic-transit-gloria"><img alt="Sic Transit Gloria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409348093p2/27914644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409570205?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sic Transit Gloria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sic Transit Gloria" href="/user/show/27914644-sic-transit-gloria">Sic Transit Gloria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409570205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9258998972047189720">EDIT: I've read the series now. It's not worth it. It just keeps getting weirder, adding more unnecessary things, and slowing down. Don't bother with it.<br/><br/>This book abides by one motto: "Make it weirder." The story starts with a duel to determine the best swordsman. I thus assumed a medieval time frame and was promptly proved wrong when the protagonist encounters a genetically locked voice recorder. The rest of the book proceeds in this fashion, introducing modern and sometimes futuristic technolo</span>
  <span id="freeText9258998972047189720" style="display:none">EDIT: I've read the series now. It's not worth it. It just keeps getting weirder, adding more unnecessary things, and slowing down. Don't bother with it.<br /><br />This book abides by one motto: "Make it weirder." The story starts with a duel to determine the best swordsman. I thus assumed a medieval time frame and was promptly proved wrong when the protagonist encounters a genetically locked voice recorder. The rest of the book proceeds in this fashion, introducing modern and sometimes futuristic technology alongside traditional fantasy elements. This facet is unexplained, introducing a pattern whereby important parts of the world aren't explained in the slightest. What is a Diviner, anyway? How big is a dragon? Why does no one carry spears?<br /><br />Ironically, the biggest fault of the book was the overabundance of useless explanations. It felt like every character had to explain the logic for every action they took. It really slows down the pacing and bores the reader.<br /><br />Still, this book does possess some major upsides. For one, it doesn't fall into the YA trap of awkwardly forcing two characters into a romance in a single book, though I suspect the rest of the series does feature a love subplot. The action (when there is action) is actually really exciting. Perhaps most importantly, the premise of the book is interesting as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9258998972047189720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8833983093506076575">This book had a strange feeling to it. And I know I won’t be able to describe it well, but it reminded me of the feeling I get from watching the desert scenes in the <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0086190/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Return of the Jedi</a>, kind of detached and barren. When his older brother goes missing, he sets out on a quest to find him and ends up discovering the myths are true.</span>
  <span id="freeText8833983093506076575" style="display:none">This book had a strange feeling to it. And I know I won’t be able to describe it well, but it reminded me of the feeling I get from watching the desert scenes in the <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0086190/" rel="nofollow noopener">Return of the Jedi</a>, kind of detached and barren. This makes no sense, I know, but it’s true. Anyway, Jason has grown up hearing myths about dragons stealing people from his world to use as slaves on their dragon world. When his older brother goes missing, he sets out on a quest to find him and ends up discovering the myths are true. Meanwhile, Koren lives on the dragon’s world as a slave. She is just discovering that she has talents as a visionary which will make the dragons fear her. Koren and Jason end up banding together to combine their talents to save the slaves. This is part one of four.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165354435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12963872904071520787">I recieved this as a Christmas gift. I loved Bryan Davis's Dragons in our Midst/Oracles of Fire series, so I was excited to get into another dragon series by him!<br/><br/>The premise of this book was really unique. The setting was strange, but I liked it. I also liked how Davis wove together the stories of Jason and Koren. Speaking of Jason, he reminds me very much of Billy Bannister from DIOM. Hm.... I liked the characters, as a whole. They were very well-developed, and I actually cared about them. <br/><br/>Over</span>
  <span id="freeText12963872904071520787" style="display:none">I recieved this as a Christmas gift. I loved Bryan Davis's Dragons in our Midst/Oracles of Fire series, so I was excited to get into another dragon series by him!<br /><br />The premise of this book was really unique. The setting was strange, but I liked it. I also liked how Davis wove together the stories of Jason and Koren. Speaking of Jason, he reminds me very much of Billy Bannister from DIOM. Hm.... I liked the characters, as a whole. They were very well-developed, and I actually cared about them. <br /><br />Overall, this was an exciting read that I really enjoyed. I need to read the next one, now!<br /><br />Sorry about the incredibly short review. I'm behind. <br /><br /><br />Read even more reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com">http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com</a>!</span>

<div id="review_338280372" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/338280372" />
    <a title="Kara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6137018-kara"><img alt="Kara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482283420p2/6137018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/338280372?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara" href="/user/show/6137018-kara">Kara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer338280372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10550777243321706043">Starlighter by Bryan Davis<br/>Review by Kara Grant<br/>Minor Spoilers<br/><br/><br/>My Review<br/>Jason Masters is a peasant boy whose life consists of lessons, training, tournaments, and tasks in the commune. He is a trained warrior who wants more out of life. He longs to slay dragons and rescue slaves, both of which are rumors and thought not to exist. He lives with his parents and older brother, Adrian, who is also Jason’s training coach and mentor.<br/><br/>Koren is an orphan slave who lives with other orphans that serve dragons.</span>
  <span id="freeText10550777243321706043" style="display:none">Starlighter by Bryan Davis<br />Review by Kara Grant<br />Minor Spoilers<br /><br /><br />My Review<br />Jason Masters is a peasant boy whose life consists of lessons, training, tournaments, and tasks in the commune. He is a trained warrior who wants more out of life. He longs to slay dragons and rescue slaves, both of which are rumors and thought not to exist. He lives with his parents and older brother, Adrian, who is also Jason’s training coach and mentor.<br /><br />Koren is an orphan slave who lives with other orphans that serve dragons. She has no chance of getting promoted because she has red hair and green eyes and is too valued by her slave drivers to ever be released. She is a known storyteller with the power to hypnotize any dragons in observing her tales. She is also kind, considerate, and very wise due to all the suffering she has witnessed and experienced. She takes a walk one night hoping to find answers for her friend and everything changes.<br /><br />Wow, what a story! It’s slow to start out with, but quickly picks up and has the reader drawn in as the characters figure out their next steps throughout their journeys. When the story begins, Jason is fighting in a tournament against the governor’s son and wants to advance to the finals. He longs to bring recognition to his commune with his fighting skills. His brother is present at first, but then alerts Jason to a secret assignment he must accept. In his absence, Jason has been given Adrian’s job serving as the governor’s bodyguard before Adrian leaves. Jason has only been on the job one day when everything changes and he is forced to find out the truth about rumored dragons and human slaves. Adrian is not presumed missing until near the end of the story when much of the mystery has been solved. <br /><br />There are no mention of dragons for the first 50 pages, only references and implications at first. Even though plenty of dragons come into the story later, only a few are mentioned by name. The main part of the story is the teens as they discover hidden truths, corruption, and deceptions passed down for centuries. I didn’t understand every bit of it, but I was eager to see how each conflict got resolved. Several times throughout the book, I thought, How are they going to get out of this one??!! I was not disappointed :)<br /><br />There is a lot of magic, the animals all talk, and even though the young ones have to deal with lots of despair, the story always has tangible hope and faith throughout. There is one talking bear, one ghost-like being, and the dragons speak their own language as well as the human language. There is also religion briefly mentioned in the story. One of the main dragons is a priest and he defends his faith more than once to the other dragons when they believe him to be superstitious and farfetched. He is loyal to the dragon heritage, but he is also compassionate to the young humans and admirably helps them several times. The other religion mentioned is the Zodiac Cathedral where the cries of “spiritual transformations” can be heard (only referred to, no details are given).<br /><br />I also learned that dragons never keep living plants in their caves. The only green they like are green emeralds and green-eyed slaves.<br />There is one dragon egg containing a dragon prince that Koren is chained to in order to prove her skills. He is one of the main dragons, but only his egg gets described. He has the ability to communicate through the egg and is deceptive as well as manipulative. He only wants to be loved and served, but in a forceful manner (made me think of the movie Sphere with Dustin Hoffman).<br /><br />There is lots of violence in the story, but nothing graphic or scary. Jason and Koren experience equal amounts of violence and tension; they are both tested several times in the story. Jason gets struck by lightning, fights with a bear, drowns at one point and kills one dragon. Two girls get to ride a dragon in the story, THAT was cool! The human slaves are all ages; abused, mistreated, judged, scorned, whipped, tortured, and constantly forced to submit to the dragons. Adults are constantly threatened that their kids will be placed as cattle children when they don’t cooperate or make their quotas for the day. Cattle children are forced to work without being fed properly and basically starve to death or catch diseases from lack of care. <br /><br />Towards the end of the story, Jason, Koren and their friends must fight dragons, flooding, and bees before reaching safety. Jason and Koren have special instincts that serve them well in the story and they constantly take risks to save others. That was my favorite part of the story. These kids are blessed and favored because of their selfless deeds, that’s how I saw the story. They are surrounded by traitors, but they never seek revenge. They value their lives and have strong wills, but they only desire to rescue the human slaves and bring freedom to the captives. That’s the kind of story I never get tired of reading :)<br /> <br />This is an amazing story filled with heroic characters, cowardly villains, deceptive lineage/history, and teenagers willing to risk everything to restore order to human civilization. It was difficult reading about the slavery in this book because this has happened and still goes on in our world today, but it was well written and became a motivator within the plot. There are also brief references to a Creator who is loving and merciful, Koren prays in the story. This story reminded me of The Lord of the Rings the way it plays out. It’s fantasy with lots of action and a quest to discover truth and bring justice, but it also has Christian symbolism. It’s the first book in a series, but it can be a stand alone also. It has an incomplete ending because it’s implied more of the story is dealt with in the sequel. I highly recommend this book to anyone looking for a story filled with friendship, sacrifice, honor, great villains, magic, greed, hope, and flying dragons that talk! For more information about Bryan Davis, please see his website: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.daviscrossing.com/index.htm">http://www.daviscrossing.com/index.htm</a> <br /><br />I want to thank Zondervan for sending me a review paperback copy. I was not required to write a positive review. The opinions I have expressed are my own.<br />*please see my blog for a giveaway, karathewriter.blogspot.com*</span>
  <a data-text-id="10550777243321706043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5441091255371187131">The Dragons of Starlight Series by Bryan Davis is the first series where I have (so far - I'm two books in) no idea what is going to happen. Literally, I had no guesses for anything. And I love that feeling! I wonder it will be like re-reading it (and I know I will, this series is too good to only read once).<br/>This is a great start to this exciting series! I couldn't put this book down! This is a thrilling story with humorous parts, Biblical morals, great role models, unforgettable characters, and</span>
  <span id="freeText5441091255371187131" style="display:none">The Dragons of Starlight Series by Bryan Davis is the first series where I have (so far - I'm two books in) no idea what is going to happen. Literally, I had no guesses for anything. And I love that feeling! I wonder it will be like re-reading it (and I know I will, this series is too good to only read once).<br />This is a great start to this exciting series! I couldn't put this book down! This is a thrilling story with humorous parts, Biblical morals, great role models, unforgettable characters, and terrible injustices that make you wish you could enter the world to make things right.<br />As I read this book, I could almost see it all taking place around me, like ghostly starlighter images.<br />This book is completely clean, no language, no romance, no graphic violence, no occultism or witchcraft (though a gifted character is accused of being a witch).<br />I can't wait to finish reading this thrilling series!</span>

<div id="review_103418784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103418784" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3451586-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483310497p2/3451586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103418784?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/3451586-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3451586-leah?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3451586-leah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3451586-leah?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3451586-leah?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103418784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8869407295631601370"> <br/> Starlighter tells a vivid tale of two groups of people on different planets destined to find each other. One group, The Lost Ones, are slaves on a planet taken over by dragons. The dragons have enslaved them for so many generations that they are unaware that they come from a different planet where humans rule and dragons are considered mythical.<br/><br/> The story starts out with the character, Jason, defeating Randall, son of the governor, in a sword fighting challenge. Soon after they find themselves</span>
  <span id="freeText8869407295631601370" style="display:none"> <br /> Starlighter tells a vivid tale of two groups of people on different planets destined to find each other. One group, The Lost Ones, are slaves on a planet taken over by dragons. The dragons have enslaved them for so many generations that they are unaware that they come from a different planet where humans rule and dragons are considered mythical.<br /><br /> The story starts out with the character, Jason, defeating Randall, son of the governor, in a sword fighting challenge. Soon after they find themselves running for their lives, fighting talking bears and laser fire. There's upheaval in their country's leadership and Jason has been framed for murder. They rescue Elyssa from prison, gain a new friend, Tibault and continue on the run until they find the entrance to the dragon world. The four of them work to open the portal to the other world to rescue the Lost Ones they've heard tales about.<br /><br /> Meanwhile, Koren, is a slave in the lost world who possesses the ability to hypnotize dragons with her storytelling. She is working to rescue her friend, Natalla, from her "promotion" by the dragons. They never know if the dragons are killing their promoted ones or truly setting them free. Koren has a close relationship with the dragon she serves, Arxad, who helps her deceive the other dragons without them thinking he's on her side. Koren has been tested and declared a Starlighter, someone who can see the future and speak with the unhatched dragon prince. When Koren and Natalla escape with the help of Arxad, they run to the mines where Jason's group meets up with them . The story reaches it's peak intensity here....Do they make it to the safe world? Do they stay in the dragon world and have Jason and Randall protect them? Will the slaves even believe another world exists or turn them over to the dragons to spare their own lives?<br /><br /> Excerpt: <br /><br /> "Koren, you must gather your wits. it is imperative that we fly immediately. If you are found out, I can no longer protect you."<br /><br /> In the midst of the swirling lights, a dragon's face orbited with them. She murmured, "Found out?"<br /><br /> "You are a Starlighter, and you are far more powerful than the one Magnar expected."<br /><br /> "How..." She licked her dry lips. Her throat felt parched. "How do you know?"<br /><br /> "You made Darksphere brighten and come to life. The previous Starlighter did the same, but she revealed the humans' origins with only a little detail."<br /><br /> "You mean, you knew we came from Darksphere?"<br /><br /> "Of course I knew, but the tale you told differs greatly from Magnar's version."<br /><br />(and)<br /><br /> "If you are able, you must climb on my back. I will take you to the Northlands. There lives someone who might be able to help."<br /><br /> "The Northlands?" A shot of excitement worked to focus Koren's brain. "So there really is such a place? Promoted humans really go there?"<br /><br /> "There is such a place." Arxad lowered his head. "Now mount quickly."<br /><br />My first impression was COVER-LOVE! The yellow dragon eyes peering over the redhaired girl, who is peering over a large black egg implore you to start wondering. Her eyes challenge you to ask what is she going to do with this egg? The intensity of the cover is delivered in the story. It winds several story lines together, action, some violence, colorful characters, original ideas and adventure all in one. I loved reading Koren's moments when the powerful dragons would be mesmerized by her storytelling. Also towards the end of the book the characters suddenly start referring to their Creator, comparing how loving and merciful he was in opposition to being forced to love the dragon prince in it's egg shell. <br /><br />Excerpt: <br /><br /> Magnar's growl deepened. "we will follow you to the ends of Starlight. You would never have a moment's peace. And when the prince hatches, what will you do? Will you murder him: or will you, like most humans, consider his life more valuable once you can see him?<br /> This story had so much going on in the beginning, that I was a little confused when I got to the middle. There were so many characters to follow. However, I loved the original imagery Bryan Davis put into the story. After reading the scenes where the characters fly on Arxad, I actually dreamt that I was flying on him! Wow! The third portion of the book is intense and even a little edgy, but riddled with compassion, survival, and personal sacrifice. The last portion of the book mentions the character's belief in her creator and how he loves with mercy as opposed to the dragon prince forcing her to love him. I would have liked the characters to have mentioned their beliefs earlier on in the story, more as a continuous thread since it has a lot of bearing on the way the story plays out at the end. <br /><br /> This is a great story for an older middle grade reader, a young adult, as well as an adult young at heart. For the Christian reader that enjoys stories of dragons without all the sorcery, this one keeps it to a minimum. It's a clean book, although some strong imagery makes it more appropriate for older kids.<br /><br /><br />Starlighter is the first in the Dragons of Starlight Series and is available at Amazon here. Be watching for book two Warrior in January 2011!<br /><br /><br />I give this book **** (four stars)!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8869407295631601370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2850457979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2850457979" />
    <a title="Jason McGhee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40817795-jason-mcghee"><img alt="Jason McGhee" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2850457979?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason McGhee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason McGhee" href="/user/show/40817795-jason-mcghee">Jason McGhee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8549952-starlighter">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2850457979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14573031654363747676"><strong>Amazing story and fantastic characters</strong><br/><br/>Bryan Davis does a fantastic job with Starlighter! The flow of the story with the likable characters keep you glued to page after page. The book has great meanings of struggle, triumph, friendship, love, and compassion. A great read and I can't wait to continue the story and enjoy this amazing journey!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vABPH3ndGFrOIgp+t8SYKbyQznzQfEMNz/in8WlEKgqqpU40p7wdDZqox7xYmFmkFBlK8XY8ZwlUCcdPqqBIHQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t9yZrMA8roCyf3lkduxRBg/dCL0wHHw6vIO8bnhLT9mheZiHHl2r1+b1tKaZsJCLp1SMMJZcWD4nctzQu68tzg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Now, trained by the King himself, Leinad returns—a true Knight of the King. His skill with the sword is unmatched this side of the Great Sea ; his resolve is unshakeable. He is determined to fulfill the mission given him by the King and to free the people from their bondage to Lord Fairos. Leinad’s quest takes him from the chains of slavery, near the jaws of dragons, and close to the arms of love. And when the rest of the kingdom turns away from the King and the Code, Leinad turns to his most faithful ally, Tess. With her help, Leinad struggles to conquer his own doubt. But he must do so soon, for the King’s archenemy, the Dark Knight, is about to unleash his entire evil force, and only Leinad can stop them… Journey to Arrethtrae, where the King and His Son implement a bold plan to save their kingdom; where courage, faith, and loyalty stand tall in the face of opposition; where good will not bow to evil; where the future of the kingdom is at the threshold of either victory or defeat—and one man holds the key. DISCUSSION QUESTIONS INCLUDED Story Behind the Book“When my six kids’ eyes glossed over during a reading from the Bible, I paused to explain the significance of redemption to a sin-sick soul. I was rewarded with patronizing elephant nods and more blank stares. Shortly thereafter, I awoke in the middle of the night with a medieval story enveloping my mind. I wrote it down and later read it to my children. Their waning attention transformed into complete anticipation. I was amazed and disappointed. Why did it take a fictional story, not a Bible passage, to get that response? Then I realized—that is how Jesus taught! Parables are powerful! I penned the Kingdom series to help young people get excited about the supremely significant story of Jesus Christ and His mission to save mankind.” —Chuck Black<\/span>\n  <a After many years, Kingdom’s Edge finds Cedric living a hopeless life until a stranger appears with powerful words of a new kingdom and a grand army. Swords, knights, and battles define these captivating tales that parallel biblical events from Genesis to Revelation! He was doomed to a life of hopelessness and despair.  Then the stranger arrived…  For Cedric of Chessington, every day is the same: full of poverty and despair. And he knows that will never change. Or so he thinks. Then a stranger comes to the city. Drawn to the man’s mysterious ways, Cedric discovers the stranger’s humility belies great strength and wisdom. That’s when an astounding truth becomes clear—the stranger is a Master of the Sword, and He is there to train Cedric. Suddenly propelled into a desperate battle against evil, Cedric must rely on the Master’s training if he is going to survive. But the ultimate battle is yet to come, for the Dark Knight is at work, implementing his plan to take over the kingdom. Will Cedric be ready to stand in the face of pure evil? Journey to Arrethtrae, where the King and His Son implement a bold plan to save their kingdom; where courage, faith, and loyalty stand tall in the face of opposition; where good will not bow to evil; and where hope and compassion are as powerful weapons as the sword. DISCUSSION QUESTIONS INCLUDED Story Behind the Book“When my six kids’ eyes glossed over during a reading from the Bible, I paused to explain the significance of redemption to a sin-sick soul. I was rewarded with patronizing elephant nods and more blank stares. Shortly thereafter, I awoke in the middle of the night with a medieval story enveloping my mind. I wrote it down and later read it to my children. Their waning attention transformed into complete anticipation. I was amazed and disappointed. Why did it take a fictional story, not a Bible passage, to get that response? Then I realized—that is how Jesus taught! Parables are powerful! I penned the Kingdom series to help young people get excited about the supremely significant story of Jesus Christ and His mission to save mankind.” — Chuck Black<\/span>\n  <a
